CASE_ID: 001
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: cardiology

DIAGNOSIS:
Hypertrophic Cardiomyopathy

ALIASES:
HCM
hypertrophic obstructive cardiomyopathy
HOCM

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. An 18-year-old male collapses suddenly during a basketball game and is resuscitated.
2. His father died unexpectedly at age 40 from an unknown cardiac cause.
3. A harsh crescendo-decrescendo systolic murmur is heard at the left sternal border that intensifies with Valsalva.
4. ECG shows left ventricular hypertrophy with deep narrow Q waves in the lateral leads.
5. Echocardiography reveals asymmetric septal hypertrophy with systolic anterior motion of the mitral valve.
6. Genetic testing reveals a pathogenic MYH7 mutation, and an ICD is implanted given his resuscitated cardiac arrest.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- HCM is the most common cause of sudden cardiac death in young athletes.
- The murmur increases with maneuvers that decrease preload (Valsalva, standing) and decreases with squatting.
- Most cases are autosomal dominant mutations in sarcomere genes such as MYH7 and MYBPC3.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 002
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: cardiology

DIAGNOSIS:
Aortic Stenosis

ALIASES:
AS
calcific aortic stenosis
severe aortic stenosis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 74-year-old man reports exertional chest pain, dizziness, and one episode of syncope while climbing stairs.
2. He has a long history of hypertension and hyperlipidemia.
3. A harsh late-peaking systolic ejection murmur radiates to the carotids with diminished and delayed carotid upstrokes.
4. ECG shows left ventricular hypertrophy with a strain pattern.
5. Echocardiography shows a heavily calcified valve with a mean gradient of 48 mmHg.
6. He undergoes TAVR, and intraoperative findings confirm a severely calcified tricuspid aortic valve with a final valve area of 0.7 cm2.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- The classic triad of symptomatic aortic stenosis is angina, syncope, and heart failure.
- In patients over 70, calcific degeneration of a normal trileaflet valve is the most common cause.
- Onset of symptoms marks a sharp decline in prognosis and is an indication for valve replacement.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 003
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: cardiology

DIAGNOSIS:
Cardiac Tamponade

ALIASES:
pericardial tamponade
tamponade

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 58-year-old woman presents with worsening shortness of breath and fatigue over two weeks.
2. She was diagnosed with metastatic lung adenocarcinoma three months ago.
3. Examination reveals hypotension, muffled heart sounds, distended neck veins, and a pulsus paradoxus of 18 mmHg.
4. ECG shows low voltage QRS complexes with electrical alternans.
5. Echocardiography demonstrates a large pericardial effusion with diastolic collapse of the right ventricle.
6. Pericardiocentesis removes 480 mL of hemorrhagic fluid, and cytology reveals malignant cells consistent with metastatic lung cancer.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Beck triad consists of hypotension, distended neck veins, and muffled heart sounds.
- Pulsus paradoxus is an exaggerated drop in systolic blood pressure greater than 10 mmHg during inspiration.
- Electrical alternans reflects the swinging motion of the heart within a fluid-filled pericardial sac.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 004
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: cardiology

DIAGNOSIS:
Acute ST-Elevation Myocardial Infarction

ALIASES:
STEMI
acute MI
heart attack

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 62-year-old man develops sudden crushing substernal chest pressure radiating to his left arm with diaphoresis.
2. He has a 40-pack-year smoking history and type 2 diabetes.
3. He appears diaphoretic and anxious with an S4 gallop on auscultation.
4. ECG shows ST-segment elevation in leads II, III, and aVF.
5. Bedside echocardiography shows hypokinesis of the inferior wall.
6. Coronary angiography reveals 100% occlusion of the right coronary artery, and a drug-eluting stent is placed with restoration of flow.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Inferior wall MIs are most often caused by right coronary artery occlusion.
- Troponin is the most sensitive and specific biomarker for myocardial injury.
- Time to reperfusion is critical, and primary PCI is preferred when available within 90 minutes.

CASE_ID: 005
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: cardiology

DIAGNOSIS:
Infective Endocarditis

ALIASES:
bacterial endocarditis
IE

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 32-year-old man presents with five days of fever, chills, and malaise.
2. He has a history of intravenous heroin use.
3. Examination reveals a new holosystolic murmur at the left lower sternal border and painless erythematous macules on his palms.
4. Blood cultures grow Staphylococcus aureus in three of three bottles.
5. Transesophageal echocardiography shows a mobile vegetation on the tricuspid valve.
6. Repeat cultures remain positive over 48 hours, and the patient is started on a six-week course of IV antibiotics for confirmed tricuspid valve endocarditis.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Right-sided endocarditis in injection drug users most commonly involves the tricuspid valve.
- Staphylococcus aureus is the most common cause of acute infective endocarditis.
- The Duke criteria are used to establish the diagnosis based on major and minor findings.

CASE_ID: 006
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pulmonology

DIAGNOSIS:
Pulmonary Embolism

ALIASES:
PE
acute pulmonary embolism
venous thromboembolism

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 55-year-old woman presents with sudden-onset pleuritic chest pain and shortness of breath.
2. She returned yesterday from a 12-hour transatlantic flight and takes oral contraceptives.
3. She is tachycardic and tachypneic with an oxygen saturation of 89% on room air and a swollen tender right calf.
4. Arterial blood gas shows hypoxemia with a respiratory alkalosis, and D-dimer is markedly elevated.
5. CT pulmonary angiography reveals a filling defect in the right main pulmonary artery.
6. Lower extremity ultrasound confirms a deep vein thrombosis in the right femoral vein, and the patient is started on therapeutic anticoagulation.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Virchow triad describes the three contributors to thrombosis: stasis, endothelial injury, and hypercoagulability.
- The most common ECG finding in PE is sinus tachycardia, though S1Q3T3 is classically described.
- CT pulmonary angiography is the gold standard diagnostic test in hemodynamically stable patients.

CASE_ID: 007
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pulmonology

DIAGNOSIS:
Chronic Obstructive Pulmonary Disease

ALIASES:
COPD
emphysema
chronic bronchitis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 66-year-old man complains of progressive shortness of breath and a chronic productive cough for years.
2. He has smoked one pack of cigarettes daily for 45 years.
3. He has a barrel-shaped chest, prolonged expiration, and diffuse wheezing on auscultation.
4. Arterial blood gas shows chronic CO2 retention with a compensated respiratory acidosis.
5. Chest X-ray shows hyperinflated lungs with flattened diaphragms and increased retrosternal air space.
6. Spirometry reveals an FEV1/FVC ratio of 0.58 that does not improve significantly with bronchodilators, confirming irreversible airflow obstruction.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- COPD is defined by airflow limitation that is not fully reversible, distinguishing it from asthma.
- Smoking cessation is the single most effective intervention to slow disease progression.
- A reduced FEV1/FVC ratio below 0.70 is the spirometric hallmark of obstructive disease.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 008
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pulmonology

DIAGNOSIS:
Community-Acquired Pneumonia

ALIASES:
CAP
pneumococcal pneumonia
lobar pneumonia

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 48-year-old man presents with three days of high fever, productive cough with rust-colored sputum, and right-sided chest pain.
2. He recently recovered from an upper respiratory infection.
3. Examination reveals dullness to percussion, bronchial breath sounds, and increased tactile fremitus over the right lower lobe.
4. Sputum Gram stain shows lancet-shaped gram-positive diplococci.
5. Chest X-ray reveals a dense right lower lobe consolidation with air bronchograms.
6. Sputum culture grows Streptococcus pneumoniae, and the patient improves on empiric ceftriaxone and azithromycin.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Streptococcus pneumoniae is the most common cause of community-acquired pneumonia.
- Rust-colored sputum is classically associated with pneumococcal infection.
- The CURB-65 score helps determine the need for hospitalization.

CASE_ID: 009
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pulmonology

DIAGNOSIS:
Asthma

ALIASES:
bronchial asthma
reactive airway disease

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 24-year-old woman presents with recurrent episodes of wheezing, chest tightness, and cough that worsen at night.
2. She has a history of eczema and seasonal allergic rhinitis.
3. Examination during an episode reveals diffuse expiratory wheezing and a prolonged expiratory phase.
4. Peak expiratory flow is reduced, and CBC shows mild eosinophilia.
5. Chest X-ray during an acute episode shows hyperinflation without focal consolidation.
6. Spirometry shows obstruction with greater than 12% improvement in FEV1 after bronchodilator administration, confirming reversible airflow limitation.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Asthma is characterized by reversible airway obstruction, bronchial hyperresponsiveness, and inflammation.
- The atopic triad consists of asthma, eczema, and allergic rhinitis.
- Reversibility of obstruction with bronchodilators distinguishes asthma from COPD.

CASE_ID: 010
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pulmonology

DIAGNOSIS:
Sarcoidosis

ALIASES:
pulmonary sarcoidosis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 35-year-old African American woman presents with several weeks of dry cough, fatigue, and mild dyspnea.
2. She also reports tender red nodules on her shins and blurred vision.
3. Examination reveals erythema nodosum on the lower extremities and anterior uveitis on slit-lamp exam.
4. Serum calcium and angiotensin-converting enzyme levels are elevated.
5. Chest X-ray shows bilateral hilar lymphadenopathy.
6. Transbronchial biopsy reveals noncaseating granulomas, and stains for acid-fast bacilli and fungi are negative.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Sarcoidosis is a diagnosis of exclusion characterized by noncaseating granulomas.
- Hypercalcemia results from increased 1-alpha-hydroxylase activity in granulomas producing active vitamin D.
- It most commonly affects young African American women and shows bilateral hilar lymphadenopathy.

CASE_ID: 011
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: gastroenterology

DIAGNOSIS:
Acute Pancreatitis

ALIASES:
pancreatitis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 45-year-old man presents with severe epigastric pain radiating to the back, with nausea and vomiting.
2. He admits to heavy alcohol use over the past weekend.
3. Examination reveals epigastric tenderness, abdominal guarding, and decreased bowel sounds.
4. Serum lipase is elevated to more than three times the upper limit of normal.
5. Contrast-enhanced CT of the abdomen shows an edematous pancreas with peripancreatic fat stranding.
6. The patient improves with aggressive IV fluids and bowel rest, and his lipase trends down over several days confirming resolving pancreatitis.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Gallstones and alcohol are the two most common causes of acute pancreatitis.
- Lipase is more specific than amylase for pancreatic injury.
- Aggressive fluid resuscitation is the cornerstone of early management.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 012
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: gastroenterology

DIAGNOSIS:
Crohn Disease

ALIASES:
Crohn's disease
regional enteritis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 27-year-old woman presents with months of crampy abdominal pain, non-bloody diarrhea, and unintended weight loss.
2. She reports intermittent mouth ulcers and joint pains.
3. Examination reveals a tender right lower quadrant fullness and perianal skin tags.
4. Labs show anemia, elevated CRP, and low vitamin B12.
5. CT enterography shows skip lesions with bowel wall thickening in the terminal ileum.
6. Colonoscopy with biopsy reveals transmural inflammation with noncaseating granulomas in a cobblestone mucosal pattern.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Crohn disease can affect any part of the GI tract from mouth to anus with skip lesions.
- Transmural inflammation predisposes to fistulas, strictures, and abscesses.
- Terminal ileum involvement causes malabsorption of vitamin B12 and bile acids.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 013
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: gastroenterology

DIAGNOSIS:
Ulcerative Colitis

ALIASES:
UC

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 30-year-old man presents with several weeks of bloody diarrhea with mucus and lower abdominal cramping.
2. He reports a frequent sensation of incomplete evacuation and urgency.
3. Examination reveals mild lower abdominal tenderness without masses.
4. Labs show anemia and elevated inflammatory markers, with p-ANCA positivity.
5. CT shows continuous colonic wall thickening extending proximally from the rectum.
6. Colonoscopy reveals continuous mucosal inflammation with friability and pseudopolyps, and biopsy shows crypt abscesses limited to the mucosa.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Ulcerative colitis involves continuous inflammation starting at the rectum and extending proximally.
- Inflammation is limited to the mucosa and submucosa, unlike the transmural disease of Crohn.
- Primary sclerosing cholangitis is an associated extraintestinal manifestation.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 014
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: gastroenterology

DIAGNOSIS:
Hereditary Hemochromatosis

ALIASES:
hemochromatosis
iron overload

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 52-year-old man presents with fatigue, joint pain, and decreased libido.
2. He has noticed a bronze discoloration of his skin and was recently diagnosed with diabetes.
3. Examination reveals hepatomegaly and hyperpigmentation of the skin.
4. Labs show elevated serum ferritin and a transferrin saturation of 78%.
5. MRI of the liver demonstrates iron deposition with decreased signal intensity.
6. Genetic testing confirms homozygosity for the C282Y mutation in the HFE gene.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Hereditary hemochromatosis is an autosomal recessive disorder of iron absorption due to HFE mutations.
- The classic triad is cirrhosis, diabetes, and skin hyperpigmentation, called bronze diabetes.
- Therapeutic phlebotomy is the mainstay of treatment.

CASE_ID: 015
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: gastroenterology

DIAGNOSIS:
Celiac Disease

ALIASES:
celiac sprue
gluten-sensitive enteropathy

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 29-year-old woman presents with chronic diarrhea, bloating, and unintentional weight loss.
2. She notes her symptoms worsen after eating bread and pasta.
3. Examination reveals an itchy vesicular rash on the extensor surfaces of her elbows.
4. Labs show iron deficiency anemia and positive anti-tissue transglutaminase IgA antibodies.
5. Capsule endoscopy shows scalloping of the duodenal folds.
6. Duodenal biopsy reveals villous atrophy, crypt hyperplasia, and intraepithelial lymphocytosis that improve on a gluten-free diet.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Celiac disease is an autoimmune reaction to gliadin in genetically susceptible individuals (HLA-DQ2/DQ8).
- Dermatitis herpetiformis is the characteristic skin manifestation.
- Biopsy of the distal duodenum showing villous atrophy is the diagnostic gold standard.

CASE_ID: 016
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: endocrinology

DIAGNOSIS:
Graves Disease

ALIASES:
Graves' disease
toxic diffuse goiter
hyperthyroidism

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 33-year-old woman presents with palpitations, heat intolerance, weight loss despite increased appetite, and anxiety.
2. She reports her eyes appear more prominent and her neck has become fuller.
3. Examination reveals exophthalmos, a diffuse nontender goiter with a bruit, and a fine resting tremor.
4. Labs show suppressed TSH with elevated free T4 and positive thyroid-stimulating immunoglobulin.
5. Radioactive iodine uptake scan shows diffusely increased uptake throughout the gland.
6. The presence of pretibial myxedema and stimulating TSH receptor antibodies confirms autoimmune Graves disease.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Graves disease is caused by IgG autoantibodies that stimulate the TSH receptor.
- Exophthalmos and pretibial myxedema are specific extrathyroidal manifestations.
- Diffusely increased radioactive iodine uptake distinguishes it from toxic nodular disease and thyroiditis.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 017
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: endocrinology

DIAGNOSIS:
Diabetic Ketoacidosis

ALIASES:
DKA

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 19-year-old man presents with one day of nausea, vomiting, abdominal pain, and rapid breathing.
2. He was recently diagnosed with type 1 diabetes and ran out of his insulin.
3. Examination reveals deep rapid Kussmaul respirations and a fruity odor on his breath.
4. Labs show glucose of 480 mg/dL, anion gap metabolic acidosis, and positive serum ketones.
5. There is no acute finding on chest imaging to suggest an alternative cause.
6. Arterial pH is 7.18 with a bicarbonate of 12, and the patient improves with IV fluids, an insulin infusion, and potassium repletion.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- DKA is characterized by hyperglycemia, anion gap metabolic acidosis, and ketosis.
- Total body potassium is depleted despite a normal or high serum level, requiring careful repletion.
- IV fluids and insulin are the cornerstones of treatment, with glucose monitoring to avoid hypoglycemia.

CASE_ID: 018
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: endocrinology

DIAGNOSIS:
Cushing Syndrome

ALIASES:
hypercortisolism
Cushing's syndrome

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 44-year-old woman presents with progressive weight gain, easy bruising, and muscle weakness.
2. She reports new purple stretch marks on her abdomen and worsening hypertension.
3. Examination reveals central obesity, a dorsocervical fat pad, moon facies, and wide violaceous abdominal striae.
4. Labs show hyperglycemia and elevated late-night salivary cortisol with failure to suppress on low-dose dexamethasone.
5. Pituitary MRI reveals a small adenoma.
6. High-dose dexamethasone suppresses cortisol and ACTH is elevated, confirming a pituitary source of ACTH-dependent hypercortisolism.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Cushing disease specifically refers to an ACTH-secreting pituitary adenoma.
- The most common overall cause of Cushing syndrome is exogenous glucocorticoid use.
- High-dose dexamethasone suppression distinguishes pituitary adenomas from ectopic ACTH sources.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 019
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: endocrinology

DIAGNOSIS:
Primary Hyperparathyroidism

ALIASES:
hyperparathyroidism
parathyroid adenoma

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 56-year-old woman is found to have an elevated calcium level on routine bloodwork.
2. She reports fatigue, constipation, increased thirst, and a recent kidney stone.
3. Examination is largely unremarkable without a palpable neck mass.
4. Labs show hypercalcemia with an inappropriately elevated PTH and low phosphate.
5. A sestamibi scan localizes a single hyperfunctioning parathyroid gland.
6. Surgical resection reveals a solitary parathyroid adenoma, and intraoperative PTH falls by more than 50% after removal.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- A solitary parathyroid adenoma is the most common cause of primary hyperparathyroidism.
- Symptoms are remembered as stones, bones, groans, and psychiatric overtones.
- High calcium with high PTH distinguishes primary hyperparathyroidism from other causes of hypercalcemia.

CASE_ID: 020
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: endocrinology

DIAGNOSIS:
Pheochromocytoma

ALIASES:
pheo
adrenal medullary tumor

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 41-year-old man presents with episodic pounding headaches, palpitations, and profuse sweating.
2. He reports these spells come on suddenly and resolve over half an hour.
3. During an episode his blood pressure is 210/120 mmHg with tachycardia and pallor.
4. Plasma free metanephrines and 24-hour urine metanephrines are markedly elevated.
5. CT of the abdomen reveals a 4 cm right adrenal mass.
6. After alpha-blockade and surgical resection, pathology confirms a catecholamine-secreting tumor of chromaffin cells.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Pheochromocytoma follows the rule of 10s: 10% bilateral, 10% malignant, 10% extra-adrenal.
- The classic triad is episodic headache, sweating, and tachycardia.
- Alpha-blockade must precede beta-blockade to avoid unopposed alpha stimulation and hypertensive crisis.

CASE_ID: 021
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: neurology

DIAGNOSIS:
Multiple Sclerosis

ALIASES:
MS

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 28-year-old woman presents with one week of blurred vision and pain in her right eye with movement.
2. She recalls an episode of arm numbness and weakness last year that resolved spontaneously.
3. Examination reveals an afferent pupillary defect and internuclear ophthalmoplegia.
4. Lumbar puncture shows oligoclonal bands in the cerebrospinal fluid.
5. MRI of the brain reveals multiple periventricular white matter lesions oriented perpendicular to the ventricles.
6. A follow-up MRI months later shows new enhancing lesions, confirming dissemination in time and space.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- MS is an autoimmune demyelinating disease of the CNS with lesions separated in time and space.
- Optic neuritis is a common presenting symptom.
- Oligoclonal bands in the CSF and periventricular plaques on MRI support the diagnosis.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 022
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: neurology

DIAGNOSIS:
Myasthenia Gravis

ALIASES:
MG

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 36-year-old woman presents with drooping eyelids and double vision that worsen toward the end of the day.
2. She reports difficulty chewing and a weak voice after prolonged talking.
3. Examination reveals fatigable ptosis that worsens with sustained upgaze.
4. Serum testing is positive for acetylcholine receptor antibodies.
5. CT of the chest reveals an anterior mediastinal mass consistent with a thymoma.
6. Repetitive nerve stimulation shows a decremental response, and symptoms improve dramatically after edrophonium administration.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Myasthenia gravis is caused by autoantibodies against postsynaptic acetylcholine receptors.
- Symptoms characteristically worsen with use and improve with rest.
- Thymic abnormalities, including thymoma and hyperplasia, are commonly associated.

CASE_ID: 023
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: neurology

DIAGNOSIS:
Guillain-Barre Syndrome

ALIASES:
GBS
acute inflammatory demyelinating polyradiculoneuropathy

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 40-year-old man presents with progressive symmetric weakness in his legs ascending over several days.
2. He had a diarrheal illness two weeks ago.
3. Examination reveals symmetric lower extremity weakness with absent deep tendon reflexes.
4. Lumbar puncture shows elevated protein with a normal cell count.
5. Nerve conduction studies show demyelination with reduced conduction velocities.
6. The patient develops declining respiratory function requiring monitoring of vital capacity, and improves with IVIG, consistent with post-infectious GBS following Campylobacter.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Guillain-Barre syndrome is an acute immune-mediated demyelinating polyneuropathy, often post-infectious.
- Campylobacter jejuni is the most commonly identified preceding infection.
- Albuminocytologic dissociation (high protein, normal cells) in the CSF is characteristic.

CASE_ID: 024
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: neurology

DIAGNOSIS:
Bacterial Meningitis

ALIASES:
meningitis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 20-year-old college student presents with a severe headache, high fever, and neck stiffness for one day.
2. He lives in a crowded dormitory and several classmates have been ill.
3. Examination reveals nuchal rigidity, photophobia, and positive Kernig and Brudzinski signs.
4. Lumbar puncture shows high opening pressure, high protein, low glucose, and neutrophilic pleocytosis.
5. Head CT prior to LP shows no mass or midline shift.
6. CSF Gram stain reveals gram-negative diplococci, and culture grows Neisseria meningitidis.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Bacterial meningitis shows low glucose, high protein, and neutrophil-predominant pleocytosis in the CSF.
- Neisseria meningitidis is common in young adults in close quarters such as dormitories.
- Empiric antibiotics should not be delayed and dexamethasone reduces neurologic complications.

CASE_ID: 025
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: neurology

DIAGNOSIS:
Parkinson Disease

ALIASES:
Parkinson's disease
idiopathic parkinsonism

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 68-year-old man presents with a tremor in his right hand that is most noticeable at rest.
2. His wife notes he has become slower in his movements and his handwriting has shrunk.
3. Examination reveals a pill-rolling resting tremor, cogwheel rigidity, bradykinesia, and a shuffling gait.
4. Routine labs and metabolic workup are unremarkable.
5. MRI of the brain shows no structural lesion or vascular cause.
6. Symptoms improve substantially with a trial of levodopa, supporting a diagnosis of dopaminergic nigrostriatal degeneration.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Parkinson disease results from loss of dopaminergic neurons in the substantia nigra pars compacta.
- The classic features are resting tremor, rigidity, bradykinesia, and postural instability.
- Lewy bodies containing alpha-synuclein are the pathological hallmark.

CASE_ID: 026
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: nephrology

DIAGNOSIS:
Poststreptococcal Glomerulonephritis

ALIASES:
PSGN
acute glomerulonephritis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 7-year-old boy presents with dark cola-colored urine and puffiness around his eyes.
2. He had a sore throat about two weeks ago that resolved on its own.
3. Examination reveals periorbital edema and a blood pressure elevated for his age.
4. Urinalysis shows hematuria with red blood cell casts and mild proteinuria, with low serum C3.
5. Renal ultrasound shows normal-sized kidneys without obstruction.
6. Antistreptolysin O titers are elevated, and renal biopsy would show subepithelial humps on electron microscopy.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- PSGN classically follows group A streptococcal pharyngitis or skin infection by one to several weeks.
- It presents as a nephritic syndrome with hematuria, hypertension, and edema.
- Subepithelial immune complex humps and low complement are characteristic.

CASE_ID: 027
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: nephrology

DIAGNOSIS:
Minimal Change Disease

ALIASES:
MCD
lipoid nephrosis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 4-year-old boy presents with progressive swelling of his face, legs, and abdomen.
2. His parents note his urine has been frothy.
3. Examination reveals periorbital edema, pitting lower extremity edema, and ascites.
4. Urinalysis shows massive proteinuria, and serum albumin is low with elevated lipids.
5. Renal ultrasound is unremarkable.
6. The child responds rapidly to corticosteroids, and electron microscopy would reveal diffuse effacement of podocyte foot processes.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Minimal change disease is the most common cause of nephrotic syndrome in children.
- Light microscopy is normal, but electron microscopy shows foot process effacement.
- It is highly responsive to corticosteroid therapy.

CASE_ID: 028
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: nephrology

DIAGNOSIS:
Acute Tubular Necrosis

ALIASES:
ATN

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 64-year-old man develops decreased urine output two days after major abdominal surgery complicated by hypotension.
2. He received IV contrast and aminoglycosides during his hospitalization.
3. Examination reveals mild volume overload with bibasilar crackles.
4. Labs show rising creatinine, and urinalysis reveals muddy brown granular casts with a high fractional excretion of sodium.
5. Renal ultrasound shows no hydronephrosis or obstruction.
6. Urine sodium is greater than 40 and FENa exceeds 2%, consistent with intrinsic tubular injury rather than a prerenal cause.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Acute tubular necrosis is the most common cause of intrinsic acute kidney injury.
- Ischemia and nephrotoxins such as aminoglycosides and contrast are common causes.
- Muddy brown granular casts and high FENa distinguish ATN from prerenal azotemia.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 029
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: nephrology

DIAGNOSIS:
Autosomal Dominant Polycystic Kidney Disease

ALIASES:
ADPKD
polycystic kidney disease

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 38-year-old man presents with flank pain, blood in his urine, and difficult-to-control hypertension.
2. His father required dialysis and died of a brain aneurysm rupture.
3. Examination reveals bilateral palpable flank masses.
4. Labs show mild renal insufficiency and hematuria.
5. Abdominal ultrasound reveals numerous bilateral renal cysts with markedly enlarged kidneys.
6. Genetic testing reveals a pathogenic PKD1 mutation, and MR angiography screening detects a small berry aneurysm.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- ADPKD is most often caused by mutations in PKD1 on chromosome 16.
- Extrarenal manifestations include berry aneurysms, hepatic cysts, and mitral valve prolapse.
- It is a leading inherited cause of end-stage renal disease.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 030
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: nephrology

DIAGNOSIS:
Diabetic Nephropathy

ALIASES:
diabetic kidney disease
Kimmelstiel-Wilson disease

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 59-year-old woman with long-standing diabetes presents for routine follow-up with mild lower extremity swelling.
2. She has had type 2 diabetes for 18 years with poor glycemic control and coexisting retinopathy.
3. Examination reveals mild pitting edema and elevated blood pressure.
4. Urinalysis shows persistent albuminuria, and HbA1c is 9.2%.
5. Renal ultrasound shows normal to enlarged kidneys early in the disease.
6. Renal biopsy, if performed, would reveal nodular glomerulosclerosis with Kimmelstiel-Wilson nodules and mesangial expansion.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Diabetic nephropathy is the leading cause of end-stage renal disease in the United States.
- Persistent albuminuria is the earliest clinical sign.
- ACE inhibitors and ARBs slow progression by reducing intraglomerular pressure.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 031
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: hematology_oncology

DIAGNOSIS:
Chronic Myeloid Leukemia

ALIASES:
CML

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 50-year-old man presents with fatigue, early satiety, and abdominal fullness.
2. He has noticed drenching night sweats and unintentional weight loss.
3. Examination reveals massive splenomegaly extending toward the pelvis.
4. CBC shows marked leukocytosis with the full spectrum of myeloid maturation and a low leukocyte alkaline phosphatase score.
5. Abdominal imaging confirms an enlarged spleen.
6. Cytogenetic testing reveals the t(9;22) Philadelphia chromosome producing the BCR-ABL fusion gene, and he is started on imatinib.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- CML is defined by the BCR-ABL fusion gene from the t(9;22) translocation.
- Tyrosine kinase inhibitors such as imatinib have revolutionized treatment.
- A low leukocyte alkaline phosphatase score helps distinguish CML from a leukemoid reaction.

CASE_ID: 032
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: hematology_oncology

DIAGNOSIS:
Acute Lymphoblastic Leukemia

ALIASES:
ALL

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 5-year-old boy presents with fatigue, easy bruising, bone pain, and recurrent fevers.
2. His parents note he has been pale and less active over the past month.
3. Examination reveals pallor, scattered petechiae, hepatosplenomegaly, and lymphadenopathy.
4. CBC shows anemia, thrombocytopenia, and a high white count with circulating lymphoblasts.
5. Chest X-ray may show a mediastinal mass in the T-cell subtype.
6. Bone marrow biopsy shows greater than 20% lymphoblasts that are TdT positive, confirming acute lymphoblastic leukemia.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- ALL is the most common malignancy in children.
- TdT positivity marks lymphoblasts and distinguishes ALL from myeloid leukemias.
- The t(12;21) translocation in children carries a favorable prognosis.

CASE_ID: 033
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: hematology_oncology

DIAGNOSIS:
Multiple Myeloma

ALIASES:
MM
plasma cell myeloma

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 67-year-old man presents with progressive back pain, fatigue, and recurrent infections.
2. He reports increased thirst and constipation over recent weeks.
3. Examination reveals bony tenderness over the spine and pallor.
4. Labs show anemia, hypercalcemia, elevated creatinine, and a narrow spike on serum protein electrophoresis.
5. Skeletal survey reveals multiple punched-out lytic lesions in the skull.
6. Bone marrow biopsy shows greater than 10% clonal plasma cells, and urine contains Bence Jones proteins.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Multiple myeloma features are recalled by the CRAB mnemonic: hyperCalcemia, Renal failure, Anemia, Bone lesions.
- A monoclonal M spike on protein electrophoresis is characteristic.
- Bence Jones proteins are free monoclonal light chains found in the urine.

CASE_ID: 034
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: hematology_oncology

DIAGNOSIS:
Hodgkin Lymphoma

ALIASES:
Hodgkin's lymphoma
Hodgkin disease

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 24-year-old man presents with a painless enlarging lump in his neck for two months.
2. He reports drenching night sweats, fevers, and unexplained weight loss, with pain in the node after drinking alcohol.
3. Examination reveals firm, rubbery, nontender cervical lymphadenopathy.
4. Labs show mild anemia and an elevated ESR.
5. CT of the chest reveals mediastinal lymphadenopathy.
6. Excisional lymph node biopsy reveals Reed-Sternberg cells with an owl-eye appearance on a mixed inflammatory background.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Reed-Sternberg cells are the pathognomonic finding in Hodgkin lymphoma.
- It has a bimodal age distribution peaking in young adults and the elderly.
- Hodgkin lymphoma spreads in a contiguous, predictable fashion between lymph node groups.

CASE_ID: 035
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: hematology_oncology

DIAGNOSIS:
Sickle Cell Disease

ALIASES:
sickle cell anemia
SCD

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 9-year-old African American boy presents with sudden severe pain in his arms, legs, and back.
2. He has had similar painful episodes since early childhood, often triggered by cold or dehydration.
3. Examination reveals tenderness over the long bones, scleral icterus, and splenic atrophy.
4. CBC shows anemia with sickled cells and target cells on the peripheral smear, with elevated reticulocytes.
5. Chest X-ray during an episode of fever and hypoxia shows a new pulmonary infiltrate.
6. Hemoglobin electrophoresis reveals predominantly HbS, confirming homozygosity for the sickle mutation.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Sickle cell disease results from a glutamate-to-valine substitution in the beta-globin chain.
- Vaso-occlusive crises cause acute pain and complications such as acute chest syndrome.
- Functional asplenia from autoinfarction increases susceptibility to encapsulated organisms.

CASE_ID: 036
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: infectious_disease

DIAGNOSIS:
Tuberculosis

ALIASES:
TB
pulmonary tuberculosis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 45-year-old man presents with a chronic productive cough for six weeks, now with blood-streaked sputum.
2. He recently emigrated from a high-prevalence country and has had night sweats and weight loss.
3. Examination reveals cachexia and crackles over the upper lung fields.
4. Sputum acid-fast bacilli smear is positive, and an interferon-gamma release assay is positive.
5. Chest X-ray reveals upper lobe cavitary lesions.
6. Sputum culture grows Mycobacterium tuberculosis, and the patient is started on a four-drug regimen of rifampin, isoniazid, pyrazinamide, and ethambutol.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Reactivation tuberculosis classically involves the apical and posterior segments of the upper lobes.
- Acid-fast staining and culture confirm the diagnosis.
- The initial treatment regimen is remembered as RIPE.

CASE_ID: 037
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: infectious_disease

DIAGNOSIS:
Infectious Mononucleosis

ALIASES:
mono
EBV infection

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 19-year-old college student presents with one week of sore throat, fever, and profound fatigue.
2. She mentions kissing a partner who had similar symptoms recently.
3. Examination reveals exudative pharyngitis, posterior cervical lymphadenopathy, and splenomegaly.
4. CBC shows lymphocytosis with atypical lymphocytes, and a heterophile antibody (Monospot) test is positive.
5. Abdominal ultrasound confirms an enlarged spleen.
6. EBV-specific viral capsid antigen IgM antibodies are positive, confirming acute Epstein-Barr virus infection.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Infectious mononucleosis is most often caused by Epstein-Barr virus infecting B lymphocytes via CD21.
- Administration of amoxicillin or ampicillin classically causes a rash.
- Splenomegaly warrants avoidance of contact sports due to the risk of splenic rupture.

CASE_ID: 038
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: infectious_disease

DIAGNOSIS:
Lyme Disease

ALIASES:
Lyme borreliosis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 34-year-old man presents with fatigue, fever, and an expanding circular rash on his thigh.
2. He went hiking in wooded areas of the northeastern United States two weeks ago.
3. Examination reveals a 10 cm targetoid lesion with central clearing.
4. Early serologic testing may be negative during the acute phase.
5. There is no acute imaging abnormality on evaluation.
6. ELISA followed by confirmatory Western blot is positive for antibodies to Borrelia burgdorferi, and he responds to doxycycline.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Lyme disease is caused by Borrelia burgdorferi transmitted by the Ixodes tick.
- Erythema migrans is the characteristic early skin manifestation.
- Later complications include heart block, facial nerve palsy, and migratory arthritis.

CASE_ID: 039
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: infectious_disease

DIAGNOSIS:
Malaria

ALIASES:
Plasmodium infection

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 29-year-old woman presents with cyclical high fevers, shaking chills, and sweats every 48 hours.
2. She returned from a trip to sub-Saharan Africa three weeks ago and did not take prophylaxis.
3. Examination reveals fever, pallor, jaundice, and splenomegaly.
4. Labs show anemia, thrombocytopenia, and elevated indirect bilirubin.
5. No focal source is found on chest or abdominal imaging.
6. Thick and thin blood smears reveal intraerythrocytic ring forms and banana-shaped gametocytes consistent with Plasmodium falciparum.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Malaria is transmitted by the female Anopheles mosquito.
- Plasmodium falciparum causes the most severe disease and can cause cerebral malaria.
- Plasmodium vivax and ovale form hypnozoites requiring primaquine to prevent relapse.

CASE_ID: 040
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: infectious_disease

DIAGNOSIS:
Clostridioides difficile Colitis

ALIASES:
C. diff colitis
pseudomembranous colitis

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 70-year-old woman presents with profuse watery diarrhea and crampy abdominal pain.
2. She completed a course of clindamycin for a dental infection last week.
3. Examination reveals lower abdominal tenderness and a low-grade fever.
4. Stool testing is positive for C. difficile toxin B by PCR, and the white count is markedly elevated.
5. CT of the abdomen shows colonic wall thickening with mucosal edema.
6. Colonoscopy reveals raised yellow-white pseudomembranes on the colonic mucosa, and she improves on oral vancomycin.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- C. difficile infection commonly follows antibiotic use that disrupts normal gut flora.
- Clindamycin and fluoroquinolones are classic precipitants.
- Oral vancomycin or fidaxomicin are first-line treatments, not metronidazole for severe disease.

CASE_ID: 041
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: musculoskeletal

DIAGNOSIS:
Rheumatoid Arthritis

ALIASES:
RA

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 45-year-old woman presents with several months of symmetric pain and swelling in the small joints of her hands.
2. She reports morning stiffness lasting more than an hour that improves with use.
3. Examination reveals swelling of the metacarpophalangeal and proximal interphalangeal joints with ulnar deviation.
4. Labs show positive rheumatoid factor and anti-cyclic citrullinated peptide antibodies with elevated ESR.
5. Hand X-rays reveal periarticular osteopenia and marginal joint erosions.
6. Synovial findings of pannus formation confirm chronic inflammatory destruction of the joint.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Rheumatoid arthritis is a symmetric inflammatory polyarthritis sparing the distal interphalangeal joints.
- Anti-CCP antibodies are highly specific for the diagnosis.
- Morning stiffness improving with activity distinguishes it from osteoarthritis.

CASE_ID: 042
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: musculoskeletal

DIAGNOSIS:
Gout

ALIASES:
gouty arthritis
podagra

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 52-year-old man wakes with sudden excruciating pain, redness, and swelling of his right great toe.
2. He attended a party the night before with heavy beer and red meat consumption.
3. Examination reveals an exquisitely tender, erythematous, swollen first metatarsophalangeal joint.
4. Serum uric acid is elevated, though it may be normal during an acute attack.
5. Joint X-ray may show punched-out erosions with overhanging edges in chronic disease.
6. Arthrocentesis reveals needle-shaped, negatively birefringent crystals that appear yellow when parallel to the polarizer.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Gout results from deposition of monosodium urate crystals in joints.
- The first metatarsophalangeal joint is most commonly affected, called podagra.
- Crystals are needle-shaped and negatively birefringent under polarized light.

CASE_ID: 043
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: musculoskeletal

DIAGNOSIS:
Systemic Lupus Erythematosus

ALIASES:
SLE
lupus

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 26-year-old woman presents with fatigue, joint pain, and a facial rash that worsens with sun exposure.
2. She reports painless mouth ulcers and hair loss over recent months.
3. Examination reveals a malar rash sparing the nasolabial folds and nonerosive arthritis.
4. Labs show positive ANA and anti-double-stranded DNA antibodies with low complement levels.
5. Urinalysis reveals proteinuria and red cell casts suggesting renal involvement.
6. Renal biopsy demonstrates immune complex deposition with a wire-loop appearance, consistent with lupus nephritis.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Anti-dsDNA and anti-Smith antibodies are highly specific for SLE.
- Lupus nephritis is a major cause of morbidity and is monitored with complement and dsDNA levels.
- The malar rash characteristically spares the nasolabial folds.

CASE_ID: 044
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: musculoskeletal

DIAGNOSIS:
Osteoarthritis

ALIASES:
OA
degenerative joint disease

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 64-year-old obese woman presents with chronic knee pain that worsens with activity and improves with rest.
2. She reports brief morning stiffness lasting under 30 minutes.
3. Examination reveals bony enlargement of the distal interphalangeal joints and crepitus in the knees.
4. Inflammatory markers are normal and rheumatoid factor is negative.
5. Knee X-ray reveals joint space narrowing, subchondral sclerosis, and osteophytes.
6. The combination of weight-bearing joint involvement with Heberden nodes and absent systemic inflammation confirms degenerative joint disease.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Osteoarthritis is a noninflammatory degenerative disease driven by mechanical wear.
- Heberden nodes affect the DIP joints and Bouchard nodes affect the PIP joints.
- X-ray findings include joint space narrowing, osteophytes, and subchondral sclerosis and cysts.

CASE_ID: 045
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: psychiatry

DIAGNOSIS:
Major Depressive Disorder

ALIASES:
MDD
clinical depression

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 34-year-old woman presents with two months of persistent low mood, loss of interest in activities, and fatigue.
2. She reports difficulty sleeping, poor concentration at work, and feelings of worthlessness.
3. On mental status exam she has a flat affect, slowed speech, and poor eye contact.
4. Thyroid function tests and other labs are within normal limits.
5. There are no focal findings on neurologic examination or imaging.
6. She meets criteria with at least five depressive symptoms present nearly every day for over two weeks causing significant functional impairment.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- The diagnosis of major depression requires five or more symptoms for at least two weeks, including depressed mood or anhedonia.
- SSRIs are first-line pharmacotherapy.
- Always screen for suicidal ideation and rule out medical mimics such as hypothyroidism.

CASE_ID: 046
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: psychiatry

DIAGNOSIS:
Schizophrenia

ALIASES:
schizophrenic disorder

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 22-year-old man is brought in by his family for six months of bizarre behavior and social withdrawal.
2. They report he believes the government is broadcasting messages to him through the television.
3. On mental status exam he displays disorganized speech, paranoid delusions, and reports hearing voices commenting on his actions.
4. Toxicology screen is negative and metabolic workup is unremarkable.
5. Brain imaging shows no structural lesion.
6. He has continuous signs of disturbance for more than six months with two or more active-phase symptoms, meeting criteria for schizophrenia.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Schizophrenia requires at least six months of symptoms with one month of active-phase psychotic symptoms.
- Positive symptoms include hallucinations and delusions; negative symptoms include flat affect and avolition.
- The dopamine hypothesis underlies the efficacy of antipsychotics blocking D2 receptors.

CASE_ID: 047
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: dermatology

DIAGNOSIS:
Malignant Melanoma

ALIASES:
melanoma

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 55-year-old fair-skinned man presents with a changing mole on his back noticed by his wife.
2. He has a history of multiple blistering sunburns and uses tanning beds.
3. Examination reveals a 9 mm asymmetric pigmented lesion with irregular borders and variegated brown, black, and red coloration.
4. Dermoscopy shows an atypical pigment network and irregular streaks.
5. Imaging is reserved for staging if invasion is confirmed.
6. Excisional biopsy reveals atypical melanocytes invading the dermis with a Breslow depth of 1.8 mm.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- The ABCDEs of melanoma are Asymmetry, Border irregularity, Color variation, Diameter over 6 mm, and Evolution.
- Breslow depth is the most important prognostic factor for melanoma.
- UV exposure and fair skin are major risk factors.

CASE_ID: 048
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pediatrics

DIAGNOSIS:
Kawasaki Disease

ALIASES:
mucocutaneous lymph node syndrome

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 3-year-old boy presents with five days of high fever unresponsive to antipyretics.
2. His parents note red eyes, cracked lips, and a rash.
3. Examination reveals bilateral nonexudative conjunctivitis, a strawberry tongue, cervical lymphadenopathy, and erythema with desquamation of the hands and feet.
4. Labs show elevated inflammatory markers and thrombocytosis.
5. Echocardiography is performed to evaluate the coronary arteries and reveals early aneurysmal dilation.
6. The constellation of prolonged fever with mucocutaneous findings and coronary changes confirms Kawasaki disease, and IVIG with aspirin is started.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Kawasaki disease is a medium-vessel vasculitis and a leading cause of acquired heart disease in children.
- Coronary artery aneurysms are the most feared complication.
- Treatment with IVIG and aspirin reduces the risk of coronary complications.

CASE_ID: 049
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pharmacology

DIAGNOSIS:
Acetaminophen Toxicity

ALIASES:
acetaminophen overdose
paracetamol poisoning
Tylenol overdose

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 19-year-old woman is brought to the ED after ingesting a large quantity of pills in a suicide attempt several hours ago.
2. She initially had only mild nausea and now reports right upper quadrant pain.
3. Examination reveals right upper quadrant tenderness without jaundice initially.
4. Labs show rising AST and ALT into the thousands with a prolonged INR.
5. There is no acute imaging abnormality early in the course.
6. A serum acetaminophen level plotted on the Rumack-Matthew nomogram falls in the hepatotoxic range, and N-acetylcysteine is administered.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Acetaminophen toxicity causes centrilobular hepatic necrosis from the metabolite NAPQI depleting glutathione.
- N-acetylcysteine is the antidote and replenishes glutathione stores.
- The Rumack-Matthew nomogram guides treatment based on the level and time since ingestion.

CASE_ID: 050
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: reproductive

DIAGNOSIS:
Ectopic Pregnancy

ALIASES:
tubal pregnancy

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 28-year-old woman presents with sudden severe right lower quadrant pain and vaginal spotting.
2. Her last menstrual period was seven weeks ago and she has a history of pelvic inflammatory disease.
3. Examination reveals lower abdominal tenderness with cervical motion tenderness and a slightly enlarged adnexa.
4. A urine pregnancy test is positive, and serum beta-hCG is lower than expected for gestational age.
5. Transvaginal ultrasound shows an empty uterus with an adnexal mass and free fluid in the pelvis.
6. Laparoscopy confirms an unruptured tubal pregnancy, which is managed surgically given hemodynamic concerns.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- The ampulla of the fallopian tube is the most common site of ectopic implantation.
- Risk factors include prior PID, tubal surgery, and previous ectopic pregnancy.
- A beta-hCG that fails to rise appropriately with an empty uterus on ultrasound suggests ectopic pregnancy.

CASE_ID: 051
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: cardiology

DIAGNOSIS:
Mitral Valve Prolapse

ALIASES:
MVP
floppy mitral valve
Barlow syndrome

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 24-year-old slender woman presents with intermittent palpitations and atypical chest pain that is sharp and positional.
2. She reports occasional lightheadedness and anxiety; her symptoms have been present since her teenage years.
3. On auscultation, a mid-systolic click is heard at the apex, followed by a late systolic murmur that moves earlier with standing.
4. ECG shows isolated T-wave inversions in leads II, III, and aVF; echocardiography is ordered.
5. Echocardiography shows posterior mitral leaflet displacement more than 2 mm above the mitral annular plane with mild mitral regurgitation.
6. Genetic testing reveals a connective tissue abnormality; she is counseled on low risk of complications and referred for routine follow-up without intervention.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Most common valvular abnormality; more symptomatic in women but more complications in men over 50.
- Mid-systolic click moves earlier (toward S1) with decreased preload (standing, Valsalva) and later with increased preload (squatting).
- Complications include mitral regurgitation, infective endocarditis, arrhythmias, and rarely sudden death.

CASE_ID: 052
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: cardiology

DIAGNOSIS:
Aortic Regurgitation

ALIASES:
AR
aortic insufficiency
aortic valve regurgitation

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 38-year-old man with a known history of bicuspid aortic valve presents with progressive exertional dyspnea and awareness of his heartbeat, especially when lying down.
2. He reports a pounding sensation in his neck and chest and notes his pulse feels forceful.
3. On exam, blood pressure is 158/48 mmHg; the pulse is bounding (water-hammer pulse) and head bobbing is observed (de Musset sign).
4. Auscultation reveals a high-pitched blowing early diastolic decrescendo murmur best heard at the left sternal border with the patient leaning forward.
5. Echocardiography shows a dilated left ventricle with an end-diastolic diameter of 6.8 cm, preserved EF of 52%, and severe aortic regurgitation with a wide vena contracta.
6. Cardiac MRI confirms a regurgitant fraction of 52% and an ascending aortic diameter of 4.8 cm; surgical aortic valve replacement with root repair is planned.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Wide pulse pressure (high systolic, low diastolic) is the hemodynamic hallmark.
- Early diastolic decrescendo murmur at left sternal border; Austin Flint murmur (low-pitched mid-diastolic rumble) may coexist.
- Chronic AR causes eccentric LV hypertrophy; surgery indicated when symptomatic or EF drops below 50%.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 053
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: cardiology

DIAGNOSIS:
Complete Heart Block

ALIASES:
third degree heart block
3rd degree AV block
CHB

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 72-year-old man presents to the ED with sudden onset near-syncope, severe fatigue, and presyncope while walking to his mailbox.
2. He has a history of anterior myocardial infarction 6 years ago and takes metoprolol.
3. His heart rate on exam is 38 bpm and regular; blood pressure is 88/60 mmHg.
4. ECG shows P waves firing at 78 bpm and QRS complexes firing independently at 36 bpm with no consistent PR interval relationship (AV dissociation).
5. He develops a brief episode of loss of consciousness (Stokes-Adams attack) while being monitored in the ED.
6. A temporary transvenous pacemaker is placed emergently with immediate hemodynamic improvement; he subsequently receives a permanent dual-chamber pacemaker.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Complete AV dissociation: atria and ventricles beat independently; P waves have no relation to QRS complexes.
- Causes: inferior MI (usually transient), anterior MI (usually permanent), Lyme disease, medications, infiltrative disease.
- Stokes-Adams attacks: sudden loss of consciousness from cardiac standstill or ventricular arrhythmia.
- Treatment: atropine acutely; definitive treatment is permanent pacemaker.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 054
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: cardiology

DIAGNOSIS:
Hypertensive Emergency

ALIASES:
hypertensive crisis
malignant hypertension
hypertensive urgency

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 54-year-old man with poorly controlled hypertension presents to the ED with a severe occipital headache, blurred vision, and confusion that developed over several hours.
2. He ran out of his antihypertensive medications 2 weeks ago and has not been seen by a physician in over a year.
3. Blood pressure is 228/142 mmHg; fundoscopy reveals bilateral flame hemorrhages, cotton-wool spots, and papilledema.
4. Serum creatinine is 3.2 mg/dL (baseline 1.0); urinalysis shows 3+ protein with RBC casts.
5. Head CT shows no hemorrhage but diffuse white matter changes consistent with hypertensive encephalopathy; troponin is mildly elevated.
6. He is admitted to the ICU and started on IV labetalol with a target of reducing MAP by no more than 25% in the first hour; blood pressure gradually normalizes over 24 hours.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Hypertensive emergency: severely elevated BP with acute end-organ damage (brain, heart, kidneys, eyes).
- Hypertensive urgency: severely elevated BP without end-organ damage — lower gradually over 24-48 hours orally.
- IV agents: labetalol, nicardipine, clevidipine, sodium nitroprusside; avoid rapid correction (risk of cerebral ischemia).
- Papilledema on fundoscopy = hypertensive emergency until proven otherwise.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 055
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pulmonology

DIAGNOSIS:
Cystic Fibrosis

ALIASES:
CF
CFTR mutation

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 16-year-old boy with a history of recurrent pulmonary infections since infancy presents with worsening productive cough, increased sputum production, and a 12-pound weight loss over 3 months.
2. He requires pancreatic enzyme supplementation with meals and has had three prior hospitalizations for pulmonary exacerbations.
3. On exam, he has digital clubbing, barrel chest, diffuse expiratory wheezes, and coarse crackles at the right base.
4. Sputum culture grows mucoid Pseudomonas aeruginosa; FEV1 is 58% of predicted with an obstructive pattern.
5. Chest CT shows bronchiectasis predominantly in the upper lobes with mucus plugging and tree-in-bud opacities.
6. Genetic testing confirms compound heterozygosity for deltaF508 and G551D CFTR mutations; he is started on ivacaftor-lumacaftor with significant improvement in FEV1 at 3-month follow-up.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Autosomal recessive CFTR mutation (deltaF508 most common) on chromosome 7.
- Defective chloride channel leads to thick secretions; Pseudomonas aeruginosa is the most common organism in older patients.
- Sweat chloride >60 mEq/L is diagnostic; complications include bronchiectasis, pancreatic insufficiency, infertility (males).
- CFTR modulators (ivacaftor, lumacaftor, elexacaftor-tezacaftor-ivacaftor) have transformed treatment.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 056
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pulmonology

DIAGNOSIS:
Idiopathic Pulmonary Fibrosis

ALIASES:
IPF
pulmonary fibrosis
UIP

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 67-year-old retired shipyard worker presents with a 3-year history of progressive exertional dyspnea and a dry nonproductive cough.
2. He is a former smoker with a 30 pack-year history; he denies significant occupational dust or asbestos exposure.
3. On exam, bibasilar end-inspiratory fine crackles with a Velcro quality are present; digital clubbing is noted bilaterally.
4. Pulmonary function tests show a restrictive pattern with TLC 68% predicted, FVC 61% predicted, and severely reduced DLCO at 42%.
5. High-resolution CT shows bilateral basal-predominant honeycombing with traction bronchiectasis and subpleural reticulation in a UIP pattern; no ground-glass opacity is present.
6. Surgical lung biopsy confirms usual interstitial pneumonia with fibroblastic foci; he is started on nintedanib with counseling regarding lung transplant evaluation.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Progressive fibrotic lung disease of unknown cause; UIP pattern on HRCT is diagnostic without biopsy in appropriate clinical context.
- Velcro crackles, clubbing, restrictive pattern with low DLCO are characteristic.
- Antifibrotic agents (pirfenidone, nintedanib) slow progression; lung transplant is the only cure.
- Poor prognosis: median survival 3-5 years from diagnosis.

CASE_ID: 057
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pulmonology

DIAGNOSIS:
Lung Cancer

ALIASES:
non-small cell lung cancer
NSCLC
small cell lung cancer
SCLC
squamous cell carcinoma lung
adenocarcinoma lung

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 61-year-old man with a 45 pack-year smoking history presents with a 3-month history of hemoptysis, persistent cough, and a 20-pound unintentional weight loss.
2. He reports new onset hoarseness and right-sided shoulder pain radiating down his arm.
3. On exam, right-sided ptosis, miosis, and anhidrosis are noted (Horner syndrome); breath sounds are decreased at the right apex.
4. Chest CT shows a 5.8 cm spiculated mass in the right upper lobe with ipsilateral mediastinal adenopathy and invasion of the chest wall.
5. PET scan shows hypermetabolic activity in the right upper lobe mass, right hilar nodes, and right adrenal gland; brain MRI shows two enhancing lesions.
6. CT-guided biopsy reveals squamous cell carcinoma; molecular testing shows no actionable mutations; he is started on pembrolizumab plus platinum-based chemotherapy.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Pancoast tumor: superior sulcus tumor invading brachial plexus (shoulder/arm pain), stellate ganglion (Horner syndrome), subclavian vessels.
- Squamous cell: central, cavitating, associated with PTHrP-mediated hypercalcemia.
- Small cell: central, paraneoplastic syndromes (SIADH, Cushing, Lambert-Eaton), rapidly progressive.
- Adenocarcinoma: peripheral, most common in nonsmokers, EGFR/ALK/ROS1 mutations are targetable.

==================================================

CASE_ID: 058
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: pulmonology

DIAGNOSIS:
Obstructive Sleep Apnea

ALIASES:
OSA
sleep apnea
OSAHS

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 52-year-old obese man is referred by his wife who reports he snores loudly and she has observed him stop breathing for 30-second intervals during sleep on multiple occasions.
2. He reports excessive daytime sleepiness, morning headaches, and difficulty concentrating; he has fallen asleep while driving twice in the past year.
3. On exam, BMI is 38, neck circumference is 18 inches, and Mallampati class III airway is noted.
4. Overnight polysomnography shows an apnea-hypopnea index of 48 events per hour with oxygen desaturation nadir of 76% during obstructive events.
5. He also has new-onset hypertension, type 2 diabetes, and was recently found to have atrial fibrillation on a routine ECG.
6. CPAP titration study identifies an optimal pressure of 10 cmH2O with complete resolution of apneic events; after 3 months of CPAP compliance his blood pressure and daytime sleepiness improve significantly.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Repetitive upper airway collapse during sleep; obesity is the most important risk factor.
- AHI >15 = moderate; >30 = severe; polysomnography is the gold standard diagnostic test.
- Consequences: hypertension (most common), AFib, pulmonary hypertension, metabolic syndrome, cognitive impairment, increased motor vehicle accidents.
- Treatment: CPAP (gold standard); weight loss; surgery for selected patients.

CASE_ID: 059
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: gastroenterology

DIAGNOSIS:
Esophageal Cancer

ALIASES:
esophageal carcinoma
squamous cell carcinoma esophagus
adenocarcinoma esophagus

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 63-year-old man presents with a 4-month history of progressive dysphagia, initially to solids and now to liquids as well, with a 25-pound weight loss.
2. He has a 20-year history of gastroesophageal reflux disease and was told he had Barrett esophagus on endoscopy 5 years ago but was lost to follow-up.
3. On exam, he appears cachectic with palpable left supraclavicular lymphadenopathy (Virchow node).
4. Upper endoscopy reveals a circumferential, ulcerating mass in the distal esophagus at 38 cm; biopsy confirms moderately differentiated adenocarcinoma.
5. CT scan of the chest and abdomen shows the esophageal mass with involvement of the celiac axis lymph nodes and a 2.3 cm liver lesion.
6. PET-CT confirms hypermetabolic activity in the esophageal mass, celiac nodes, and liver lesion consistent with metastatic disease; he is referred for palliative chemotherapy with FOLFOX.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Two types: squamous cell (upper/mid esophagus, associated with alcohol and tobacco) and adenocarcinoma (lower esophagus/GEJ, associated with GERD and Barrett esophagus).
- Barrett esophagus: intestinal metaplasia of distal esophagus; requires surveillance endoscopy due to malignant potential.
- Progressive dysphagia (solids then liquids) + weight loss = esophageal malignancy until proven otherwise.
- Virchow node: left supraclavicular lymphadenopathy from abdominal/thoracic malignancy.

CASE_ID: 060
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: gastroenterology

DIAGNOSIS:
Hepatitis C

ALIASES:
HCV
hepatitis C virus
chronic hepatitis C

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 48-year-old man presents for evaluation of persistently elevated liver enzymes found incidentally on routine bloodwork.
2. He used intravenous drugs in his 20s and received a blood transfusion before 1992 following a motor vehicle accident.
3. He denies jaundice, abdominal pain, or significant alcohol use; he reports fatigue and mild right upper quadrant discomfort.
4. Labs show ALT 88 U/L, AST 64 U/L; anti-HCV antibody is positive; HCV RNA PCR confirms 2.4 million IU/mL with genotype 1a.
5. Liver elastography (FibroScan) shows significant fibrosis with a stiffness of 11.2 kPa consistent with F3 fibrosis; no cirrhosis is present.
6. He is treated with sofosbuvir-velpatasvir for 12 weeks and achieves a sustained virologic response (undetectable HCV RNA 12 weeks after completing treatment), confirming cure.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Most common blood-borne infection in the US; major risk factors: IV drug use, transfusions before 1992, tattoos, sexual transmission (less efficient).
- Most patients are asymptomatic for decades; complications include cirrhosis, hepatocellular carcinoma.
- Diagnosis: anti-HCV antibody (screening) confirmed by HCV RNA PCR (active infection).
- Direct-acting antivirals (DAAs) achieve cure rates >95%; HCV is now curable.

CASE_ID: 061
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: gastroenterology

DIAGNOSIS:
Cholangitis

ALIASES:
acute cholangitis
ascending cholangitis
Charcot triad
Reynolds pentad

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 68-year-old woman with a history of gallstones presents to the ED with fever, right upper quadrant pain, and jaundice developing over 24 hours.
2. She had a laparoscopic cholecystectomy 3 years ago but was told a small stone may have been left in the common bile duct.
3. On exam, temperature is 39.6°C, blood pressure is 84/52 mmHg, and she is confused; she is markedly jaundiced with RUQ tenderness.
4. Labs show WBC 22,000, total bilirubin 8.4 mg/dL, alkaline phosphatase 480 U/L, ALT 220 U/L, and blood cultures are drawn.
5. Right upper quadrant ultrasound shows a dilated common bile duct of 14 mm with an echogenic focus consistent with choledocholithiasis.
6. Emergency ERCP reveals a 1.2 cm stone impacted at the ampulla of Vater; sphincterotomy and stone extraction are performed with immediate biliary decompression and clinical improvement.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Charcot triad: fever, RUQ pain, jaundice — acute cholangitis.
- Reynolds pentad: Charcot triad + hypotension + altered mental status — suppurative cholangitis (life-threatening).
- Most common cause: choledocholithiasis obstructing the common bile duct.
- Treatment: IV antibiotics + urgent biliary decompression (ERCP preferred; surgery if ERCP fails).

CASE_ID: 062
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: gastroenterology

DIAGNOSIS:
Hepatic Encephalopathy

ALIASES:
portosystemic encephalopathy
liver encephalopathy

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 57-year-old man with alcoholic cirrhosis is brought to the ED by his family after 2 days of increasing confusion and personality changes.
2. He was recently started on a high-protein diet and missed two doses of his lactulose.
3. On exam, he is disoriented to time and place, has asterixis (flapping tremor) when his arms are outstretched, and faint hepatic fetor is noted.
4. Ammonia level is 188 mcmol/L; labs show hyponatremia, hypokalemia, and elevated INR of 2.6; head CT is normal with no intracranial pathology.
5. Evaluation reveals a urinary tract infection as the precipitating factor; he is started on antibiotics.
6. After treatment of the UTI, lactulose titrated to 3 soft stools per day, and rifaximin added, his mental status returns to baseline over 48 hours.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Cirrhosis leads to portosystemic shunting and impaired ammonia detoxification.
- Precipitants: infection (SBP, UTI), GI bleeding, constipation, high protein intake, electrolyte disturbances, sedatives, renal failure.
- Asterixis (liver flap): negative myoclonus, not specific to hepatic causes.
- Treatment: lactulose (goal 2-3 soft stools/day) + rifaximin; treat precipitant.

CASE_ID: 063
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: endocrinology

DIAGNOSIS:
Hypothyroidism

ALIASES:
Hashimoto thyroiditis
primary hypothyroidism
myxedema

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 42-year-old woman presents with a 6-month history of progressive fatigue, weight gain of 18 pounds, cold intolerance, and constipation.
2. She reports dry skin, diffuse hair loss, and worsening memory; her menstrual periods have become increasingly irregular and heavy.
3. On exam, reflexes show a prolonged relaxation phase; she has periorbital puffiness, a firm nontender goiter, dry cool skin, and bradycardia at 54 bpm.
4. TSH is markedly elevated at 22 mIU/L; free T4 is low at 0.3 ng/dL; CBC shows a normocytic anemia.
5. Anti-thyroid peroxidase antibodies are markedly elevated at 1,240 IU/mL consistent with autoimmune thyroiditis.
6. She is started on levothyroxine 75 mcg daily with dose titration; at 8 weeks TSH normalizes and her symptoms resolve substantially.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Hashimoto thyroiditis: most common cause in iodine-sufficient areas; anti-TPO antibodies are the hallmark.
- High TSH + low free T4 = primary hypothyroidism; low TSH + low T4 = secondary (pituitary).
- Myxedema coma: altered mental status + hypothermia; treat with IV T4 + T3 + stress-dose steroids.
- Treatment: levothyroxine (T4); monitor TSH every 6-8 weeks after dose changes.

CASE_ID: 064
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: endocrinology

DIAGNOSIS:
Diabetes Mellitus Type 2

ALIASES:
T2DM
type 2 diabetes
non-insulin dependent diabetes

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 52-year-old obese man presents for a routine physical; he reports fatigue and increased thirst for the past few months but denies polyuria or weight loss.
2. He has a family history of type 2 diabetes in both parents and a sedentary lifestyle; BMI is 34 and waist circumference is 42 inches.
3. Fasting glucose is 182 mg/dL on two separate occasions; HbA1c is 8.6%.
4. Urinalysis shows microalbuminuria; creatinine is 1.2 mg/dL; lipid panel shows elevated triglycerides and low HDL.
5. Fundoscopic exam reveals background diabetic retinopathy with dot and blot hemorrhages bilaterally; monofilament testing shows reduced sensation in both feet.
6. He is started on metformin and lifestyle modification; at 3 months HbA1c improves to 7.2%; an SGLT2 inhibitor is added given his cardiovascular risk profile.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Insulin resistance + relative insulin deficiency; strongly associated with obesity, sedentary lifestyle, family history.
- Complications: retinopathy, nephropathy, neuropathy (microvascular); MI, stroke, PAD (macrovascular).
- Metformin is first-line; SGLT2 inhibitors and GLP-1 agonists reduce cardiovascular and renal outcomes.
- Screening: HbA1c, fasting glucose, or 2-hour OGTT; screen all adults over 35 or with risk factors.

CASE_ID: 065
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: endocrinology

DIAGNOSIS:
Addison Disease

ALIASES:
primary adrenal insufficiency
adrenal crisis
Addison's disease

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 34-year-old woman presents with a 5-month history of progressive fatigue, weight loss, nausea, and an intense craving for salty foods.
2. Her skin has become progressively darker, especially in her palmar creases, lips, and gingival mucosa.
3. Blood pressure is 86/54 mmHg supine and drops further with standing; she has hyperpigmentation of skin and mucous membranes and appears thin and unwell.
4. Labs show sodium 126 mEq/L, potassium 5.9 mEq/L, glucose 58 mg/dL, and eosinophilia on CBC differential.
5. Morning cortisol is critically low at 1.8 mcg/dL; ACTH stimulation test shows a blunted cortisol response peaking at only 5.2 mcg/dL; plasma ACTH is markedly elevated at 310 pg/mL.
6. Anti-21-hydroxylase antibodies are strongly positive confirming autoimmune primary adrenal insufficiency; she is started on hydrocortisone and fludrocortisone with complete resolution of symptoms.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Primary adrenal insufficiency: destruction of adrenal cortex leading to deficiency of both cortisol and aldosterone.
- Hyperpigmentation from elevated ACTH cross-reacting with melanocortin receptors (MSH effect).
- Hyponatremia + hyperkalemia + hypoglycemia + eosinophilia are classic electrolyte findings.
- Adrenal crisis: hypotension + vomiting + fever; give IV hydrocortisone immediately.

CASE_ID: 066
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: endocrinology

DIAGNOSIS:
Syndrome of Inappropriate ADH

ALIASES:
SIADH
inappropriate antidiuretic hormone

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 71-year-old man with small cell lung cancer presents with nausea, confusion, and lethargy developing over 5 days; he is not on diuretics and has no signs of edema or dehydration.
2. His oncologist notes he recently started a new chemotherapy cycle with cyclophosphamide.
3. Serum sodium is 116 mEq/L and serum osmolality is 238 mOsm/kg; he is clinically euvolemic.
4. Urine osmolality is 640 mOsm/kg (inappropriately concentrated) and urine sodium is 52 mEq/L.
5. TSH and morning cortisol are both normal, ruling out hypothyroidism and adrenal insufficiency as contributing causes.
6. Fluid restriction to 800 mL per day is initiated with gradual sodium correction; ADH measurement confirms elevated levels consistent with ectopic ADH production from the lung tumor.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Euvolemic hyponatremia with concentrated urine and elevated urine sodium.
- Causes: SCLC (classic ectopic ADH), CNS disease, pulmonary disease, drugs (SSRIs, carbamazepine, cyclophosphamide, NSAIDs).
- Diagnosis of exclusion: normal thyroid and adrenal function required.
- Treatment: fluid restriction; hypertonic saline for severe/symptomatic (correct <10-12 mEq/L per day to avoid osmotic demyelination syndrome).

CASE_ID: 067
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: neurology

DIAGNOSIS:
Subarachnoid Hemorrhage

ALIASES:
SAH
ruptured aneurysm
thunderclap headache

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 50-year-old woman presents to the ED describing the sudden onset of the worst headache of her life that began while she was lifting grocery bags.
2. The pain was maximal at onset, reached peak intensity within seconds, and is unlike any headache she has ever experienced before.
3. On exam, she has nuchal rigidity, photophobia, and is irritable and confused; no focal neurological deficits are present.
4. Non-contrast CT head shows hyperdensity in the basal cisterns, bilateral Sylvian fissures, and the interhemispheric fissure.
5. CT angiography identifies a 7 mm saccular aneurysm at the anterior communicating artery.
6. She is admitted to the neuro-ICU; nimodipine is started for vasospasm prophylaxis and neurosurgery proceeds with microsurgical clipping of the aneurysm on hospital day 2.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Thunderclap headache: sudden, maximal at onset — must rule out SAH immediately.
- Most common cause: rupture of saccular (berry) aneurysm at circle of Willis bifurcations.
- CT is 98% sensitive within 6 hours; if CT negative but high suspicion, perform lumbar puncture (xanthochromia).
- Complications: rebleeding, vasospasm (days 4-14), hydrocephalus, hyponatremia (SIADH or cerebral salt wasting).

CASE_ID: 068
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: neurology

DIAGNOSIS:
Transient Ischemic Attack

ALIASES:
TIA
mini stroke
transient ischemic episode

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 67-year-old man with hypertension and atrial fibrillation presents after a 20-minute episode of right arm weakness and inability to speak that resolved completely before he arrived at the ED.
2. He is currently asymptomatic and neurologically intact on exam; his blood pressure is 168/94 mmHg.
3. NIHSS is 0; CT head is normal with no hemorrhage or early ischemic change; diffusion-weighted MRI shows no acute infarct.
4. ECG confirms atrial fibrillation; carotid ultrasound shows 45% stenosis of the left internal carotid artery without hemodynamic significance.
5. Echocardiography reveals a dilated left atrium with spontaneous echo contrast (smoke) in the left atrial appendage.
6. He is started on anticoagulation with apixaban for cardioembolic TIA prevention; his ABCD2 score is 5 indicating high short-term stroke risk and he is admitted for monitoring.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- TIA: focal neurological deficit from vascular cause that resolves completely within 24 hours; most resolve within 1 hour.
- Unlike TIA, DWI-positive lesion on MRI = minor stroke even if symptoms resolve.
- ABCD2 score predicts short-term stroke risk; high-risk patients should be admitted.
- Cardioembolic TIA (AFib): anticoagulation; large artery/lacunar: antiplatelets + risk factor modification.

CASE_ID: 069
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: neurology

DIAGNOSIS:
Epilepsy

ALIASES:
seizure disorder
generalized tonic-clonic seizure
temporal lobe epilepsy

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 19-year-old woman is brought to the ED after a witnessed episode of sudden loss of consciousness, generalized stiffening, rhythmic jerking of all four extremities lasting 2 minutes, followed by 30 minutes of confusion and sleepiness.
2. She reports having two similar episodes in the past year, each preceded by a strange rising sensation in her stomach and a sense of déjà vu.
3. She bit her tongue during the episode and was incontinent of urine; she is postictal and confused on arrival.
4. Blood glucose, sodium, and calcium are all normal; urine toxicology screen is negative; head CT is normal.
5. MRI of the brain shows a small area of increased T2 signal in the right hippocampus consistent with hippocampal sclerosis.
6. EEG shows right temporal interictal epileptiform discharges; she is started on levetiracetam with seizure freedom for 12 months and is referred for epilepsy surgery evaluation.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Temporal lobe epilepsy: most common focal epilepsy; aura (rising epigastric sensation, déjà vu, fear), automatisms, postictal confusion.
- Generalized tonic-clonic: loss of consciousness, tonic phase then clonic phase, tongue biting, incontinence, postictal state.
- First-line AEDs: levetiracetam, lamotrigine, valproate (avoid in women of childbearing age due to teratogenicity).
- Hippocampal sclerosis: most common pathology in temporal lobe epilepsy; may be surgically resectable.

CASE_ID: 070
DIFFICULTY: step1
SYSTEM: neurology

DIAGNOSIS:
Huntington Disease

ALIASES:
Huntington's disease
HD
chorea

VIGNETTE_LINES:
1. A 42-year-old man is referred by his family for evaluation of involuntary writhing movements of his arms and face, personality changes, and declining work performance over 3 years.
2. His father died in a psychiatric facility at age 58 after years of similar movements and dementia; the patient has three children.
3. On exam, he has choreiform movements of the face, arms, and trunk; saccadic eye movements are slow; he has executive dysfunction on cognitive testing.
4. Brain MRI shows bilateral caudate nucleus atrophy with compensatory enlargement of the lateral ventricles (boxing-glove appearance).
5. Genetic testing reveals 48 CAG trinucleotide repeats in the HTT gene on chromosome 4 (normal is fewer than 36 repeats), confirming the diagnosis.
6. He is counseled regarding the autosomal dominant inheritance and offered genetic counseling for his children; tetrabenazine is started for chorea with modest benefit.

TEACHING_POINTS:
- Autosomal dominant; HTT gene on chromosome 4; CAG trinucleotide repeat expansion (>36 = disease, >60 = juvenile onset).
- Anticipation: earlier onset in successive generations (longer CAG repeats).
- Clinical triad: chorea, psychiatric symptoms (depression, irritability), progressive dementia.
- Caudate atrophy on MRI; treatment is symptomatic only (tetrabenazine for chorea); no disease-modifying therapy exists.
